结构化输出管道：你的 Pydantic 类型即 schema，校验保证可用structured-output pipeline: your Pydantic model is the schema; validation guarantees usability

用途：信息抽取、表单填充、把 RAG 答案结构化Uses: information extraction, form-filling, structuring the RAG answer

结构化输出最实在的三类用途：① 信息抽取——把发票、合同、简历、邮件里的关键字段一次性抽成对象，替代成片的正则；② 表单填充——让 LLM 读一段对话或文档，直接产出表单/API 需要的参数对象，省掉中间的人工誊写；③ 把 RAG 答案结构化——这是和前面 30 课最直接的衔接：与其让 RAG 回一段话，不如让它回 {answer, sources, confidence}——answer 给人看，sources 让下游能溯源/展示引用，confidence 让程序能按阈值兜底（低置信就转人工或追问）。一旦答案有了结构，RAG 就从“生成一段文字”变成“返回一个可被程序消费、可校验、可监控的数据”——这才是把 RAG 接进真实系统的关键一步。
Structured output's three most concrete uses: (1) information extraction — pull the key fields from invoices, contracts, résumés, and emails into an object in one shot, replacing sheets of regex; (2) form-filling — have the LLM read a conversation or document and directly emit the argument object a form/API needs, skipping the manual transcription in between; (3) structuring the RAG answer — the most direct tie-in to the previous 30 lessons: rather than letting RAG reply with a paragraph, have it return {answer, sources, confidence} — answer for the human, sources so downstream can trace/show citations, and confidence so code can fall back on a threshold (escalate to a human or ask again when confidence is low). Once the answer has structure, RAG shifts from “generating text” to “returning data that programs can consume, validate, and monitor” — the key step to wiring RAG into a real system.
RAG 答案对象RAG answer object
answer: stranswer: str
给人读的最终回答the human-readable answer
sources: listsources: list
引用来源，可溯源、可展示cited sources — traceable, displayable
confidence: floatconfidence: float
置信度，低于阈值就兜底/转人工confidence — fall back / escalate below a threshold
把 RAG 答案从“一段话”变成可程序化消费的结构：可溯源、可校验、可按 confidence 兜底turn the RAG answer from “a paragraph” into a program-consumable structure: traceable, validatable, with confidence-based fallback
🧩 生活类比🧩 Analogy
与其让对方写一段话、你再从字里行间猜重点，不如直接递给他一张“表格”让他逐格填——栏目（字段）和格式（类型）都是你定好的，他只能照着填。结构化输出就是给 LLM 递表格：你先把 Invoice 的“厂商 / 金额 / 到期日”这几栏画好，模型不再自由发挥写小作文，而是把答案填进你的格子里，你拿到就能用。
Rather than having someone write a paragraph and then guessing the key points between the lines, hand them a “form” to fill in box by box — the columns (fields) and formats (types) are all set by you, and they can only fill them in. Structured output is handing the LLM a form: you draw the “vendor / total / due-date” columns of Invoice first, and instead of free-styling an essay the model drops its answer into your boxes, ready to use.
✅ 本课要点✅ Key points
  • 自由文本 + 正则/手工 parse 脆弱易碎：措辞一变、格式不稳、静默失败，错误一路混进下游。Free text + regex/manual parsing is brittle: wording drifts, formats wobble, failures are silent, and errors slip downstream.
  • Pydantic program：先用 BaseModel 声明形状，让 LLM 直接产出校验过的对象——类型即契约，下游 .total 拿来就用。Pydantic program: declare the shape with a BaseModel and have the LLM emit a validated object directly — the type is the contract, downstream .total just works.
  • 两条路：LLMTextCompletionProgram（prompt 塞 schema，软约束、不挑模型）vs FunctionCallingProgram（函数调用，硬约束、更稳）；structured_predict 自动按模型能力选路，且收 PromptTemplate 而非裸字符串。Two routes: LLMTextCompletionProgram (schema in the prompt, soft, model-agnostic) vs FunctionCallingProgram (function calling, hard, steadier); structured_predict auto-picks the route by model capability and takes a PromptTemplate, not a bare string.
  • 用途：信息抽取、表单填充、把 RAG 答案结构化为 {answer, sources, confidence}——让答案可消费、可校验、可监控。Uses: information extraction, form-filling, and structuring the RAG answer into {answer, sources, confidence} — making the answer consumable, validatable, monitorable.
💡 设计亮点💡 Design insight
结构化输出的精髓，是把“解析自由文本”这件脆活，换成“契约化的类型”这件稳活——类型即契约。朴素 RAG 让 LLM 写一段话、你在下游用正则去猜字段，措辞一变就碎；结构化输出反过来：你先用 Pydantic 声明结果的形状，LLM 直接产出被校验过的对象，下游 .total 拿来就用，解析这一环整个消失。要记住三件事：① 两条路按“约束有多硬”分——纯 prompt 模板（软约束、不挑模型）vs 函数调用（硬约束、更稳、要模型支持），能用函数调用就优先，而 structured_predict 会自动按模型能力选路、替你执行这条法则；② 它不是免费午餐——校验失败仍要重试/修复，schema 太复杂模型也会填错，从简单字段做起；③ 它的工程价值是“让 LLM 的输出可被程序消费”——把 RAG 答案变成 {answer, sources, confidence} 才能接监控、接兜底、接工作流。而这一步——“把 Pydantic 模型当函数签名交给模型”——正是下一部分 Agent 的地基：工具调用的参数本质就是一个 schema，“产出受约束的结构”和“调用一个工具”是同一种能力。L32 的多智能体，就是踩着结构化输出这块砖往上走的。
The essence of structured output is swapping the brittle job of “parsing free text” for the stable one of “a contracted type” — the type is the contract. Plain RAG has the LLM write a paragraph and you guess fields downstream with regex, breaking when wording shifts; structured output flips it: you declare the result's shape with Pydantic, the LLM emits a validated object directly, downstream .total just works, and the parsing step vanishes entirely. Remember three things: (1) the two routes split by “how hard the constraint is” — a pure prompt template (soft, model-agnostic) vs function calling (hard, steadier, needs model support), and prefer function calling when you can, while structured_predict auto-picks the route by model capability for you; (2) it's no free lunch — validation can still fail and need retries/repair, and an over-complex schema gets misfilled, so start from simple fields; (3) its engineering value is “making the LLM's output program-consumable” — turning the RAG answer into {answer, sources, confidence} is what lets you wire in monitoring, fallbacks, and workflows. And that very move — “handing a Pydantic model to the model as a function signature” — is the bedrock of the next part's Agents: a tool call's arguments are themselves a schema, and “emitting a constrained structure” and “calling a tool” are the same ability. L32's multi-agent systems are built standing on this structured-output brick.

🧪 自测 · 想一想为什么这么设计🧪 Self-check · think about the design

1. 为什么用 Pydantic program 而不是正则 parse LLM 的自由文本？Why use a Pydantic program instead of regex-parsing the LLM's free text?
  1. 自动获得多模态能力it automatically gains multimodal ability
  2. 完全不需要 LLMit removes the need for an LLM entirely
  3. 输出有类型校验、契约稳定，下游可直接用the output is type-validated with a stable contract, ready for downstream use
  4. 更省 tokenit saves tokens
看答案与解析Show answer & explanation 点击展开expand
答案：CAnswer: C 正确的是“输出有类型校验、契约稳定，下游可直接用”：结构化输出的价值是“类型即契约”——LLM 直接产出校验过的对象，下游 .total 拿来就用，措辞一变也不再让解析崩。“更省 token”不对——把 schema 塞进提示反而多花 token；“完全不需要 LLM”更不对——仍然要 LLM 来生成，只是把生成目标从“一段话”换成“一个对象”；“自动获得多模态能力”与结构化输出无关，那是另一回事（L29）。The right one is “the output is type-validated with a stable contract, ready for downstream use”: structured output's value is “the type is the contract” — the LLM emits a validated object directly, downstream .total just works, and shifting wording no longer breaks parsing. “It saves tokens” is wrong — stuffing the schema into the prompt actually spends more tokens; “it removes the need for an LLM entirely” is more wrong — you still need the LLM to generate, just with the target changed from “a paragraph” to “an object”; and “multimodal ability” is unrelated to structured output — that's a different topic (L29).

🎯 面试官提问 · 试着答出要点🎯 Interviewer asks · cover the key points

🎯 1. 你的结构化输出偶尔会不符合 schema——少字段、类型错、或多塞了一段解释导致解析失败。线上你会怎么兜住，让它别把脏数据放进下游？Your structured output occasionally violates the schema — a missing field, a wrong type, or an extra paragraph of explanation that breaks parsing. In production, how would you catch it so it doesn't push dirty data downstream?
看参考要点Show key points 点击展开expand
🔑 重点：校验失败就重试/修复而不是放行；能用 function-calling 模式就优先——它的约束来自模型原生能力，比纯 prompt 模板把 schema 写进提示更稳。① 校验是闸门：program 用 Pydantic 校验模型回的内容，不合格不放行——这一步本身就是“静默失败”的解药（对比 L31 痛点里手工 parse 的悄悄返回默认值）；② 失败就重试/修复：把校验错误回喂给模型让它改（“你少了 due_date 字段，请补全”），或限定重试次数后降级；③ 换更硬的约束：纯 prompt 模板是“软约束”，模型容易多写少写——改用 FunctionCallingProgram / structured_predict，让模型在函数调用层按字段产出，跑偏概率大降；④ schema 从简：字段越少越浅、类型越基础，模型越不容易填错；复杂结构先拆小再组合。一句话：校验当闸门、失败就重试、约束尽量硬、schema 尽量简。🔑 Key: on a validation failure, retry/repair rather than let it through; prefer the function-calling mode when you can — its constraint comes from the model's native ability, steadier than writing the schema into a pure prompt template. (1) Validation is the gate: the program validates the model's output with Pydantic and won't pass what fails — that step is itself the antidote to “silent failure” (vs the manual parse in L31's pain point that quietly returns a default); (2) retry/repair on failure: feed the validation error back to the model to fix it (“you're missing due_date, please complete it”), or degrade after a capped number of retries; (3) switch to a harder constraint: a pure prompt template is a “soft” constraint and the model easily over/under-writes — use FunctionCallingProgram / structured_predict so the model emits by field at the function-calling layer, sharply cutting drift; (4) keep the schema simple: fewer, shallower fields and basic types are harder to misfill; split complex structures small first, then compose. In a line: gate on validation, retry on failure, make the constraint as hard as you can, and keep the schema as simple as possible.

校验当闸门：不合格就重试/修复，绝不把脏数据放进下游validation as a gate: retry/repair on failure, never push dirty data downstream
🎯 2. 面试官追问：structured output 和 function/tool calling 是什么关系？为什么说搞懂前者就等于摸到了 Agent 工具调用的门？The interviewer presses: what's the relationship between structured output and function/tool calling, and why does grasping the former mean you've touched the door to an Agent's tool calling?
看参考要点Show key points 点击展开expand
🔑 重点：本质是同一种机制——都让模型产出“受约束的结构”；工具调用的参数本身就是一个 schema，模型“按 Pydantic 模型填字段”和“按函数签名填实参”是同一件事——这正是 L32 agent 工具调用的地基。① 同一能力，两种用法：function-calling 路线的结构化输出，就是把你的 Pydantic 模型当成一个“函数签名”交给模型，让它在 API 层产出合规的字段——这和 agent “调用一个工具”时模型要产出“该工具的入参对象”是同一套机制；② 差别只在用途：结构化输出把这个“受约束的结构”当最终结果返回给你；agent 则把它当一次工具调用的参数、拿去执行、再把结果喂回循环；③ 所以是铺垫：你在本课学会“让模型可靠地产出一个schema 对象”，到 L32 只是把这个对象接上一个可执行的工具，模型就从“填表”升级成“调工具”。一句话：结构化输出是“静态的工具调用”，工具调用是“会执行的结构化输出”。🔑 Key: they're the same mechanism — both make the model emit a “constrained structure”; a tool call's arguments are themselves a schema, and “filling a Pydantic model's fields” and “filling a function signature's arguments” are one and the same — exactly the bedrock of L32's agent tool calling. (1) One ability, two uses: the function-calling route of structured output hands your Pydantic model to the model as a “function signature” so it emits conformant fields at the API level — the same machinery an agent uses when, to “call a tool”, the model must produce “that tool's argument object”; (2) the only difference is purpose: structured output returns that “constrained structure” to you as the final result; an agent treats it as the arguments of a tool call, runs the tool, and feeds the result back into the loop; (3) hence the setup: here you learn to “make the model reliably emit a schema object”, and by L32 you simply wire that object to an executable tool, upgrading the model from “filling a form” to “calling a tool”. In a line: structured output is a “static tool call”, and a tool call is “structured output that executes”.
结构化输出Structured output
Pydantic 模型 → 模型产出受约束对象 → 当结果返回Pydantic model → model emits a constrained object → returned as the result
vs
工具调用（L32）Tool calling (L32)
函数签名 → 模型产出入参对象 → 执行工具再回喂循环function signature → model emits an argument object → run the tool, feed back into the loop
同一机制，差别只在“受约束结构”是当结果，还是当一次工具调用的参数same mechanism; the only difference is whether the constrained structure is the result or the args of a tool call
🎯 3. 什么时候不该上结构化输出？给我一个会让它“看着省事、实则添乱”的反例。When should you not reach for structured output? Give me a counter-example where it “looks convenient but actually adds trouble”.
看参考要点Show key points 点击展开expand
🔑 重点：当输出本就是给人读的自由表达（解释、写作、开放对话），或 schema 复杂多变到模型频繁填错时，硬套结构化输出只会增加重试与维护成本——结构化的收益是“下游要程序化消费”，没有这个需求就别套。① 自由表达类：让模型“解释这段代码”“写一段安抚用户的话”，答案的价值在语言本身，塞进 {summary: str} 这种壳子既没增益、还可能截断表达；② schema 过重：字段几十个、深层嵌套、还常改——模型填错率高、重试烧钱，维护 schema 比写正则还累，这时不如拆小或只structured 关键几个字段；③ 判断标准：问一句“下游是程序消费还是人消费”——程序消费（写库、触发流程、按字段分支）才值得上；人消费就让它好好说话。一句话：结构化是为“机器读”服务的，别拿它去框“人读”的内容。🔑 Key: when the output is inherently free expression for a human to read (explanations, writing, open conversation), or the schema is so complex and volatile that the model misfills it often, forcing structured output only adds retry and maintenance cost — its payoff is “downstream needs to consume it programmatically”, so without that need, don't force it. (1) Free-expression cases: “explain this code”, “write a calming note to the user” — the value is in the language itself, and cramming it into a {summary: str} shell adds nothing and may truncate the expression; (2) over-heavy schema: dozens of fields, deep nesting, frequently changing — high misfill rate, costly retries, and maintaining the schema is wearier than writing regex; better to break it down or structure only the few key fields; (3) the test: ask “is downstream a machine or a human” — machine consumption (writing to a store, triggering a flow, branching on fields) earns it; human consumption should let the model just talk. In a line: structuring serves “machine reading” — don't box in content meant for “human reading”.
💭 发散思考（没有标准答案）💭 Open questions (no single right answer)
  • 把 RAG 的答案变成 {answer, sources, confidence} 结构有什么工程价值？（提示：下游可程序化消费 / 可校验 / 可监控（如按 confidence 兜底））What is the engineering value of turning a RAG answer into a {answer, sources, confidence} structure? (Hint: programmatically consumable downstream / validatable / monitorable, e.g. fall back on confidence)
第八部分 · Agentic 进阶与上线

32 · 多智能体与控制流

写入路径Write path加载Load切块SplitEmbedEmbed存储Store索引Index
查询路径Query path检索Retrieve后处理Post-process合成Synthesize回答Answer

L26 已经把 RAG 从“写死的链”升级成“会决策的循环”——单个 agent + 一条最小 workflow。但当任务本身要跨好几种能力：先查资料、再写成答复、最后核事实，把这些工具和规则全塞进一个 agent就会乱：工具一多它越容易选错，system_prompt 要同时写“怎么查 / 怎么写 / 怎么核”越写越长越打架，出错你也分不清是哪一环。这一课往前走两步：① 把一个全能 agent 拆成几个各管一段的专精 agent，用 handoff（交接）把任务从一个传给下一个——AgentWorkflow 负责编排；② 再往底层看一层：agent 其实跑在 workflow 上，用 @step + 事件能把“分支 / 循环”这类控制流显式写出来——看得见、可单测。一句话：从“一个全能选手”升级到“一支有分工、会交接的小队”，并让这支小队的行进路线变成可检查的代码。L26 already upgraded RAG from a “hard-wired chain” to a “deciding loop” — one agent plus a minimal workflow. But when the task itself spans several capabilities — first search for facts, then write the reply, finally check the facts — cramming all those tools and rules into one agent gets messy: with many tools it more easily picks wrong, its system prompt has to say “how to search / write / check” all at once, growing long and self-contradictory, and on a failure you can't tell which part broke. This lesson takes two steps forward: (1) split one do-everything agent into several specialized agents that each own one slice, and use handoff to pass the task from one to the next — with AgentWorkflow doing the orchestration; (2) look one layer deeper: an agent actually runs on a workflow, and with @step + events you can write control flow like “branches / loops” out explicitly — visible and unit-testable. In a line: upgrade from “one all-round player” to “a small team with clear roles that hands off”, and make that team's route inspectable code.

单 agent 全包One agent does it all
查 / 写 / 核的工具和规则全塞进一个 agent：工具一多就选错，system_prompt 越写越长越打架，出错也分不清是哪一环。
all the search / write / check tools and rules crammed into one agent: many tools mean wrong picks, the system prompt grows long and self-contradictory, and failures are hard to localize.
vs
多 agent 分工 + handoffMany agents: split + handoff
每个 agent 只精一段、只配该段工具；干完用 handoff 把任务交给下一个更合适的——清晰、好测、好扩。
each agent masters one slice with only that slice's tools; when done it hands off to the next, more suitable one — clear, testable, extensible.
把“一个全能 agent”拆成“分工 + 会交接的小队”：窄职责更准，交接路线显式可控Split “one do-everything agent” into “roles + a handing-off team”: narrow duties are more accurate, handoff routes explicit and controlled

① 单 agent 不够：拆成多 agent 分工 + 交接(handoff)① One agent isn't enough: split into multiple agents with division of labor + handoff

L26 的单 agent 已经会“看问题、选工具、循环到够答”。但当任务要跨好几种能力，把工具和规则全堆在一个 agent 上，麻烦就来了：工具一多，它得在十几个里挑，选错的概率上升；system_prompt 要同时交代“怎么查、怎么写、怎么核”，越写越长、彼此打架，模型顾此失彼；真出了错，你也分不清是“查错了”还是“写跑了”。解法是分工：把一个全能 agent 拆成几个各管一段的专精 agent，每个只配它那段需要的工具、只写它那段的 system_prompt——窄而精，自然更准、更好维护。它们之间靠 handoff（交接）协作：一个 agent 干完自己那段，把控制权连同上下文交给下一个更合适的 agent，像接力赛传棒（查→写→核三个角色就能串成一条线）。要点是：handoff 不是“关掉某个工具”，也不是“换个更大的模型”，而是把任务移交给队友。
L26's single agent already “reads the question, picks a tool, and loops until it can answer”. But when the task spans several capabilities, piling all the tools and rules onto one agent invites trouble: with many tools it must choose among a dozen, so the odds of a wrong pick rise; the system prompt has to spell out “how to search, write, and check” at once, growing long and self-contradictory until the model is pulled every way; and when something breaks you can't tell whether it “searched wrong” or “wrote off-track”. The fix is division of labor: split one do-everything agent into several specialized agents that each own one slice, each wired only with the tools its slice needs and only its slice's system prompt — narrow and sharp, naturally more accurate and easier to maintain. They cooperate via handoff: one agent finishes its slice and passes control along with the context to the next, more suitable agent, like a relay baton (search→write→check threads three roles into one line). The point: a handoff is not “turning off a tool” and not “switching to a bigger model” — it is handing the task to a teammate.

② AgentWorkflow 编排多 agent：name / system_prompt / tools / can_handoff_to② AgentWorkflow orchestrates the agents: name / system_prompt / tools / can_handoff_to

把这支小队编排起来的，是 AgentWorkflow。每个成员是一个 FunctionAgent，四样东西定义它的角色：name（队友靠名字点名交接）、system_prompt（它这段的职责与风格）、tools（它能用的工具，撰稿 agent 可以一个都不带）、can_handoff_to（它允许把任务交给哪些 agent——交接路线是你显式声明的，不是模型乱传）。构造时把所有 agent 放进 agents=[...]，再指定 root_agent 作为入口（第一个接手的人）。运行 await workflow.run(user_msg=...)，root agent 先处理，需要时调用一次 handoff 把任务交给下一位——其实 handoff 在底层就是框架自动注入的一个工具，所以“交接”和 L26 的“调用工具”本质同源，只不过这次被调用的“工具”是另一个 agent。（这也正好踩在 L31 的砖上：让模型可靠产出“受约束的结构”，就是工具调用、也是 handoff 的地基。）
What orchestrates this team is AgentWorkflow. Each member is a FunctionAgent defined by four things: name (teammates hand off by name), system_prompt (its slice's duty and style), tools (the tools it may use — a writing agent can carry none), and can_handoff_to (which agents it is allowed to pass the task to — the handoff routes are declared by you, not improvised by the model). You put all agents into agents=[...] and name a root_agent as the entry (whoever takes the task first). Calling await workflow.run(user_msg=...), the root agent handles it first and, when needed, invokes one handoff to pass the task on — under the hood a handoff is just a tool the framework auto-injects, so “handing off” and L26's “calling a tool” share the same root; it's only that this time the “tool” being called is another agent. (This stands on L31's brick: making the model reliably emit a “constrained structure” is the bedrock of both tool calls and handoffs.)
三个专精 agent + handoff 链：research 查完交给 write 写草稿、write 再交给 review 复核定稿；AgentWorkflow 编排，root_agent 是入口；多 agent 下每个都要 description（handoff 据此择人）Three specialized agents + a handoff chain: research gathers and hands to write for a draft, write then hands to review to finalize; AgentWorkflow orchestrates, root_agent is the entry; in a multi-agent workflow each agent needs a description (handoff targets are chosen by it)
from llama_index.core.agent.workflow import AgentWorkflow, FunctionAgent

research = FunctionAgent(name="research", description="查资料的研究员", tools=[search_tool], llm=llm,
                         system_prompt="查资料，把要点交给 writer", can_handoff_to=["write"])
write = FunctionAgent(name="write", description="根据要点写草稿的写手", tools=[], llm=llm,
                      system_prompt="据要点写成草稿，交给 reviewer", can_handoff_to=["review"])
review = FunctionAgent(name="review", description="复核定稿的把关人", tools=[], llm=llm,
                       system_prompt="复核草稿，通过则定稿", can_handoff_to=[])
workflow = AgentWorkflow(agents=[research, write, review], root_agent="research")
resp = await workflow.run(user_msg="写一段关于 X-2000 的简报")

多智能体：按角色分工，用 handoff 把任务交给下一个专家multi-agent: split by role, hand off the task to the next specialist

③ 底层是 workflow：@step + 事件，把分支 / 循环显式写出来③ Underneath is a workflow: @step + events make branches / loops explicit

再往下看一层：L26 说过，agent 其实是一个内置了“工具循环”的 workflow。AgentWorkflow 把这套循环和 handoff 都封好了，开箱即用。但当你要的控制流不只是“循环调工具”——比如“琐碎问题直接答、复杂问题才检索”这种分支，或“没检索够就回到检索再来一轮”这种循环——就可以落到裸 Workflow，亲手把流程画清楚。写法承接 L26 的最小 workflow：每个 @step 方法吃一种事件、返回一种事件，StartEvent 进、StopEvent 出。关键升级在返回类型：当一个 step 的返回标成 Retrieved | StopEvent（联合类型），就等于声明“我这步会分叉——可能往下检索，也可能直接收尾”，框架据此把分支连进流程图。于是控制流不再藏在一长串 if/else 里，而是变成显式的事件流转：每个 step 是个纯函数式的小盒子（收什么、发什么一目了然），可以单独测试，分支和循环都画得出、测得到——这正是比“写死一个大函数”更可控的地方。
Drop one more layer: as L26 noted, an agent is really a workflow with a built-in “tool loop”. AgentWorkflow packages that loop and the handoffs for you, ready out of the box. But when the control flow you want is more than “loop and call tools” — say a branch like “answer trivial questions directly, retrieve only for complex ones”, or a loop like “if retrieval wasn't enough, go back and retrieve again” — you can drop to a raw Workflow and draw the flow by hand. The style continues L26's minimal workflow: each @step method consumes one event and returns one, StartEvent in, StopEvent out. The key upgrade is the return type: when a step is annotated to return Retrieved | StopEvent (a union), it declares “this step forks — it may retrieve or finish right here”, and the framework wires that branch into the graph. So control flow no longer hides inside a long if/else; it becomes an explicit flow of events: each step is a small functional box (clear about what it takes and emits), testable in isolation, with branches and loops you can draw and test — exactly what makes it more controllable than “one big hard-wired function”.
裸 Workflow：route 这个 @step 按问题难易返回不同事件（Retrieved 或 StopEvent）——分支被写成了可见、可测的控制流Raw Workflow: the route @step returns different events by difficulty (Retrieved or StopEvent) — the branch becomes visible, testable control flow
from llama_index.core.workflow import Workflow, step, StartEvent, StopEvent, Event

class Retrieved(Event):
    nodes: list

class RAGFlow(Workflow):
    @step
    async def route(self, ev: StartEvent) -> Retrieved | StopEvent:
        if is_trivial(ev.query):
            return StopEvent(result="直接答，无需检索")   # 分支：跳过检索
        return Retrieved(nodes=retrieve(ev.query))
StartEvent 进入StartEvent in路由 @steprouter @step
↓
分支：琐碎问题 → StopEvent 直接答branch: trivial → StopEvent
↓
否则 → Retrieved 事件 → 合成 @stepelse → Retrieved → synth @step
↓
StopEvent 出StopEvent out
workflow 用事件显式表达分支/循环——控制流看得见、可测a workflow makes branches/loops explicit as events — visible, testable control flow

④ 取舍：越多 agent / 越自由越强，但越难调、越贵④ Trade-off: more agents / more freedom is stronger, but harder to debug and pricier

能力越强，代价越实。每多一个 agent、每一次 handoff，都是又一次 LLM 决策：更多 token、更高延迟，还多了“会不会交错人、会不会在两个 agent 间反复踢皮球”这种新失败点。多 agent 也更难调——出了错你得先弄清“是哪个 agent、在哪一步、为什么这么交接”，这让 L23 的 trace 从“锦上添花”变成“必需品”。所以延续 L26 的那把尺子，按需选最低自主度：固定管道 → 单 agent → 多 agent / 裸 workflow，一级不够再上一级。判断要不要拆多 agent，就看任务能不能按角色清晰切开：能（查 / 写 / 核各管一段、要交接），拆了更清晰更好测；不能（其实一个角色几个工具就够），拆了只是徒增 handoff 的成本与不确定。一句话：先用最简单能解的那个。
The more capable, the realer the cost. Every extra agent and every handoff is another LLM decision: more tokens, higher latency, plus new failure modes — “did it hand off to the wrong one” and “are two agents ping-ponging the task back and forth”. Multi-agent is also harder to debug — on a failure you must first work out “which agent, at which step, and why it handed off that way”, which turns L23's tracing from a nice-to-have into a must-have. So keep L26's yardstick and pick the lowest autonomy that works: fixed pipeline → single agent → multi-agent / raw workflow, climbing only when a rung isn't enough. To decide whether to split into multiple agents, ask whether the task cuts cleanly along roles: if it does (search / write / check each owning a slice, with handoffs), splitting is clearer and more testable; if it doesn't (one role with a few tools really suffices), splitting just adds handoff cost and uncertainty. In a line: use the simplest thing that solves it.

适合Best for一个角色、几个工具够用one role, a few tools suffice任务能按角色清晰拆分、要交接task splits cleanly by role, needs handoffs要显式的分支 / 循环 / 并行控制流explicit branch / loop / parallel control flow
怎么协作How they cooperate内置工具循环a built-in tool loophandoff 在 agent 间传任务handoff passes the task between agents事件在 @step 间流转events flow between @steps
控制流Control flow藏在工具循环里hidden in the tool loop交接路线由 can_handoff_to 声明handoff routes declared via can_handoff_to显式可见：联合返回即分支explicit, visible: a union return is a branch
代价Cost多轮工具调用multiple tool-calling turns每次 handoff 多一次 LLM 决策、更难追谁干的each handoff is one more LLM decision; harder to trace who did what要自己写事件连线，但最可控可测you wire the events yourself, but it's the most controllable and testable
🧩 生活类比🧩 Analogy
单 agent 像一个样样都会的全能选手：一个人要查资料、写稿、还要自己校对，事情一多就顾此失彼。多 agent 像一支有分工的小队：调研员只管查、撰稿员只管写、审校员只管挑错，每人手里的活窄而精，干完自己那段就把接力棒（handoff）连同笔记交给下一位。而 workflow 就像这支小队写在白板上的流程图：先做什么、什么情况下跳过哪步、什么情况下返工重来——路线画明白了，哪一步出问题一眼就能定位，也能单独演练。
A single agent is like one all-round player who must research, draft, and proofread alone — overwhelmed once there's a lot to do. Multi-agent is like a team with clear roles: the researcher only gathers, the writer only writes, the reviewer only catches mistakes; each person's slice is narrow and sharp, and when done they pass the baton (handoff) — along with their notes — to the next. A workflow is that team's flowchart on a whiteboard: what to do first, when to skip a step, when to loop back and redo — with the route drawn out, you can spot exactly where a step breaks and even rehearse it in isolation.
✅ 本课要点✅ Key points
  • 单 agent 工具 / 职责堆太多就乱；拆成多个专精 agent、用 handoff（交接）把任务传给下一个更合适的。One agent with too many tools / duties gets messy; split into multiple specialized agents and use handoff to pass the task to the next, more suitable one.
  • AgentWorkflow 编排多 agent：每个 FunctionAgent 有 name / system_prompt / tools / can_handoff_to，root_agent 是入口。AgentWorkflow orchestrates the agents: each FunctionAgent has name / system_prompt / tools / can_handoff_to, and root_agent is the entry.
  • agent 底层跑在 workflow 上；用 @step + 事件把分支 / 循环这类控制流显式写出来——看得见、每步可单测（联合返回类型即分支）。An agent runs on a workflow; use @step + events to make control flow like branches / loops explicit — visible and unit-testable per step (a union return type is a branch).
  • 取舍：agent 越多、越自由越强，但每次 handoff 多一次 LLM 决策——更慢、更贵、更难调；先用最简能解的（固定管道 → 单 agent → 多 agent）。Trade-off: more agents and more freedom are stronger, but each handoff is another LLM decision — slower, pricier, harder to debug; use the simplest thing that works (fixed pipeline → single agent → multi-agent).
💡 设计亮点💡 Design insight
多智能体与控制流的精髓，是把 L26 的“一个会决策的 agent”再拆开、再摊平：拆开成一支有分工、会 handoff 的小队（AgentWorkflow 编排，每个 agent 只精一段、按 can_handoff_to 把任务交给下一位），摊平成一张显式的事件流程图（裸 Workflow 用 @step + 事件把分支 / 循环写成看得见、可单测的控制流）。两步都在解同一个问题：当任务复杂到一个 agent 的提示词和工具都装不下时，与其把复杂性塞进一个黑箱，不如把它拆成可命名、可观测、可测试的小块。但更强从来不是免费的——多一个 agent 就多一次 LLM 决策、多一处可能跑偏，调试也从“看一个 agent”变成“看一支队伍怎么交接”，因此越 agentic 越离不开 L23 的 trace。真正的判断不是“能不能上多 agent”，而是“这个任务配不配得上多 agent 的代价”：能按角色干净拆开、且确实需要交接，才拆；否则一个 agent、甚至一条固定管道，往往又快又稳。还有一道绕不开的关：当这支自由的小队要去删数据、下订单、发邮件这类高风险动作时，光靠它们自己拍板就太冒险了——得有人能在回路里喊停、点头确认。那正是下一课 L33 人在回路（HITL）要补上的“刹车”。
The essence of multi-agent and control flow is to take L26's “one deciding agent” and both split it apart and flatten it out: split into a team with roles that hands off (AgentWorkflow orchestrates; each agent masters one slice and passes the task on per can_handoff_to), and flatten into an explicit event flowchart (a raw Workflow uses @step + events to write branches / loops as visible, unit-testable control flow). Both moves solve the same problem: when a task grows too complex for one agent's prompt and tools to hold, rather than stuffing the complexity into one black box, break it into named, observable, testable pieces. But more power is never free — each extra agent is another LLM decision and another place to drift, and debugging shifts from “watching one agent” to “watching a team hand off”, so the more agentic you go, the more you lean on L23's tracing. The real call isn't “can we use multi-agent” but “is this task worth multi-agent's cost”: split only when the work cuts cleanly along roles and genuinely needs handoffs; otherwise a single agent — or even a fixed pipeline — is often faster and steadier. And one gate is unavoidable: when this free-roaming team goes to delete data, place orders, or send email — high-risk actions — letting them decide alone is too risky; someone must be able to step into the loop, halt, and confirm. That's the “brake” the next lesson, L33 Human-in-the-Loop (HITL), adds.

🧪 自测 · 想一想为什么这么设计🧪 Self-check · think about the design

1. AgentWorkflow 里的 handoff 指什么？What does a handoff mean in AgentWorkflow?
  1. 压缩对话历史省 tokencompress the conversation history to save tokens
  2. 把当前任务移交给另一个更合适的 agenthand the current task to another, more suitable agent
  3. 关闭某个工具的调用disable calling a particular tool
  4. 给 agent 切换更大的模型switch the agent to a bigger model
看答案与解析Show answer & explanation 点击展开expand
答案：BAnswer: B handoff 是多 agent 协作的核心——一个 agent 干完自己那段，把控制权和上下文交给下一个专精 agent；它与关工具、压历史、换模型都无关。把任务“移交给更合适的 agent”才是它的本义：底层框架其实把 handoff 实现成一个自动注入的工具，被调用的“工具”是另一个 agent。“关闭某个工具的调用”是改工具集、“压缩对话历史省 token”是省上下文成本、“切换更大的模型”是换 LLM——三者都不是把任务交接给队友。A handoff is the core of multi-agent cooperation — one agent finishes its slice and passes control and context to the next, specialized agent; it has nothing to do with disabling a tool, compressing history, or switching models. Its real meaning is “handing the task to a more suitable agent”: under the hood the framework implements a handoff as an auto-injected tool whose “tool” is another agent. “Disable calling a tool” edits the toolset, “compress history to save tokens” trims context cost, and “switch to a bigger model” swaps the LLM — none of them hand the task off to a teammate.

🎯 面试官提问 · 试着答出要点🎯 Interviewer asks · cover the key points

🎯 1. 你把客服 RAG 从单 agent 改成多 agent（调研 / 撰写 / 审校三个 agent + handoff）：能力更强，但也更难控。上线后你怎么评测和调试这套多 agent 系统——既看答得对不对，也看交接对不对、有没有多花钱？You turned your support RAG from a single agent into a multi-agent setup (research / write / review agents + handoff): more capable, but harder to control. After launch, how do you evaluate and debug it — checking not just whether answers are right, but whether handoffs are right and whether it overspends?
看参考要点Show key points 点击展开expand
🔑 重点：给每一次 handoff 和工具调用都加 trace（呼应 L23），把“谁、在第几步、为什么交接”记下来；评测要落到任务级 / 端到端成功率，而不是只看某一步对不对。① 先让它可观测：多 agent 是黑箱叠黑箱，必须在每次 handoff 和工具调用上打点——记录交接前后的 agent、传过去的上下文、每个 agent 用了哪些工具，否则出错你连“是哪个 agent 干的”都不知道。② 评端到端，而非单步：用 L22 的金标集看整条链的 Correctness / Faithfulness——用户只在乎最终答案，单个 agent 答得漂亮但交接时丢了上下文，整体照样错。③ 评交接行为：统计交接对不对（该交给审校却交给了撰写？）、交接次数分布、有没有在两个 agent 间反复踢皮球。④ 评成本：每问的 LLM 调用次数、token、p95 延迟，和单 agent 基线对比——每次 handoff 都是又一次 LLM 调用，要确认这份钱花得值。🔑 Key: instrument every handoff and tool call with traces (echoing L23), recording “who, at which step, and why it handed off”; evaluate at the task / end-to-end level, not just whether one step was right. (1) Make it observable first: multi-agent is a black box stacked on black boxes, so tap every handoff and tool call — log the agents before / after a handoff, the context passed across, and which tools each agent used; otherwise on a failure you can't even tell “which agent did it”. (2) Evaluate end-to-end, not per step: use L22's gold set for Correctness / Faithfulness over the whole chain — the user only cares about the final answer; one agent answering nicely but dropping context on handoff still makes the whole thing wrong. (3) Evaluate handoff behavior: track whether handoffs are correct (handed to write when it should have gone to review?), the distribution of handoff counts, and any ping-ponging between two agents. (4) Evaluate cost: LLM calls per question, tokens, p95 latency, versus the single-agent baseline — each handoff is another LLM call, so confirm the spend is worth it.

🎯 2. 为什么 LlamaIndex 的 Workflow 要用“事件驱动的 @step”来表达控制流，而不是直接写一长串 if-else？这对调试和测试意味着什么？Why does LlamaIndex's Workflow express control flow with “event-driven @step” instead of a long chain of if-else? What does that mean for debugging and testing?
看参考要点Show key points 点击展开expand
🔑 重点：事件驱动把分支 / 循环从“藏在一个大函数里的 if-else”显式化成事件——每个 @step 收一种事件、发一种事件，于是每步都能单独单测、中间事件能流式观测，整条控制流画得出、测得到。① 控制流变成数据：一个 step 把返回类型标成 Retrieved | StopEvent，就等于把“这里会分叉”写进了类型；框架据此连图，分支不再埋在缩进里。② 每步可单测：每个 step 是“输入事件 → 输出事件”的纯函数式小盒子，可以单独喂一个事件、断言它发出的事件，不必把整条链跑起来——这是一长串 if-else 很难做到的。③ 可观测 / 可干预：事件在 step 间流转，框架能流式吐出中间事件，你能实时看到“走到哪一步、产出了什么”，也方便插入 / 重排 / 并行新步骤（如加一步校验或重排）。④ 一句话：if-else 把流程焊死在控制流里，事件把流程摊开成可观察的数据流——后者天然更好测、更好维护。🔑 Key: event-driven turns branches / loops from “if-else buried in one big function” into explicit events — each @step consumes one event and emits one, so every step is unit-testable in isolation, intermediate events are streamable / observable, and the whole control flow is drawable and testable. (1) Control flow becomes data: a step annotated to return Retrieved | StopEvent writes “this forks” into the type; the framework wires the graph from that, so the branch no longer hides in indentation. (2) Each step is unit-testable: every step is a pure-functional box of “input event → output event”, so you can feed it one event and assert the event it emits without running the whole chain — hard to do with a long if-else. (3) Observable / interceptable: events flow between steps, the framework can stream intermediate events, you see in real time “which step we're on and what it produced”, and it's easy to insert / reorder / parallelize steps (e.g. add a validation or re-rank step). (4) In a line: if-else welds the process into control flow, while events spread it into an observable data flow — the latter is naturally more testable and maintainable.
一长串 if-elseone long if-else
分支埋在缩进里，要测某条路得把整个函数跑起来；改一处易牵连全局。branches hide in indentation; testing one path means running the whole function, and one change can ripple everywhere.
vs
事件驱动 @stepevent-driven @step
分支显式为事件，每个 step 单独可测、中间事件可观测、步骤可插入 / 重排。branches are explicit events; each step is independently testable, intermediate events observable, steps insertable / reorderable.
同一套分支 / 循环：if-else 焊死在函数里，事件摊开成可测、可观测的数据流Same branches / loops: if-else welds them into a function; events spread them into a testable, observable data flow
🎯 3. 多 agent 自由地互相 handoff，可能交接给错的 agent、来回踢皮球、甚至绕圈不收敛，把延迟和成本打爆。设计和上线时你怎么防，又怎么验证它不会失控？Agents handing off freely may hand off to the wrong agent, ping-pong back and forth, or even loop without converging, blowing up latency and cost. How do you prevent this in design and at launch, and how do you verify it won't run away?
看参考要点Show key points 点击展开expand
🔑 重点：给这支小队设“护栏”——用 can_handoff_to 收窄交接路线、设最大步数 / 超时 / 成本预算、做循环检测，并把高风险动作隔离（呼应 L25、铺垫 L33）；上线靠 trace + 一组“刁钻用例”回归来验证不失控。① 收窄路线：can_handoff_to 只声明确有必要的交接，别让每个 agent 都能交给所有人——路线越少越不容易乱。② 硬性上限：最大交接 / 步数、超时、token 预算，越界就停下并降级（转固定管道或礼貌兜底）。③ 循环检测：同样的 handoff 在两个 agent 间反复出现就熔断。④ 高风险动作隔离：删除、下单、发信这类绝不让 agent 自己拍板（这正是 L33 要补的人在回路）。⑤ 怎么验证：维护一组容易诱发多次交接的刁钻用例纳入回归，断言交接次数、成本、是否答对都在阈值内；线上监控每问步数与成本的 p95，越界即告警。🔑 Key: give the team “guardrails” — narrow handoff routes with can_handoff_to, set a max-step / timeout / cost budget, add loop detection, and isolate high-risk actions (echoing L25, setting up L33); verify with traces plus a regression suite of “tricky” cases. (1) Narrow the routes: have can_handoff_to declare only the handoffs that are genuinely needed; don't let every agent hand off to everyone — fewer routes, less chaos. (2) Hard caps: max handoffs / steps, timeout, token budget; on breach, stop and degrade (fall back to a fixed pipeline or a polite default). (3) Loop detection: trip a breaker when the same handoff recurs between two agents. (4) Isolate high-risk actions: deletion, ordering, sending mail must never be the agent's own call (exactly the human-in-the-loop L33 adds). (5) How to verify: keep a regression suite of cases that easily trigger many handoffs, asserting handoff count, cost, and correctness stay within thresholds; in production, monitor the p95 of steps and cost per question and alert on breach.
💭 发散思考（没有标准答案）💭 Open questions (no single right answer)
  • 什么时候该从单 agent 升级到多 agent？（提示：单 agent 工具 / 职责过载、prompt 太杂 / 任务能按角色清晰拆分 / 需要不同专精、不同 system_prompt）When should you upgrade from a single agent to multiple agents? (Hint: one agent's tools / duties are overloaded and its prompt is a mess / the task splits cleanly by role / you need different specialties and different system prompts)
第八部分 · Agentic 进阶与上线

33 · 人在回路 HITL

写入路径Write path加载Load切块SplitEmbedEmbed存储Store索引Index
查询路径Query path检索Retrieve后处理Post-process合成Synthesize回答Answer

上一课的多 agent 小队很能干，也很自由——它可能自己决定去删库、转账、下单、对外发消息。这些动作不可逆：错了就收不回来，光靠模型自己拍板太冒险。人在回路（HITL）就是给这种高风险动作装一道刹车：在真正动手前暂停，把请求交给人，等人点头才继续、摇头就中止。关键不是“每一步都要人盯”——那会把系统拖垮——而是只在不可逆 / 高风险的那一步加闸，其余照常自动。LlamaIndex 把这件事做得很轻：workflow 里某个 @step 返回一个 InputRequiredEvent 就自动“挂起并向人请求输入”，调用方从事件流里取到它、回一个 HumanResponseEvent，消费该事件的 @step 据此恢复或中止——一来一回，干净利落。Last lesson's multi-agent team is capable — and very free: it might decide on its own to drop a database, transfer money, place an order, or message the outside world. Those actions are irreversible: once wrong you can't take them back, and letting the model alone make the call is too risky. Human-in-the-loop (HITL) puts a brake on such high-risk actions: pause right before acting, hand the request to a human, and continue only on a yes — abort on a no. The point is not “a human watches every step” — that would grind the system to a halt — but to gate only the irreversible / high-risk step, leaving the rest automatic. LlamaIndex makes this light: a @step in a workflow that returns an InputRequiredEvent automatically “pauses and asks a human”; the caller picks it up from the event stream and sends back a HumanResponseEvent, and the @step consuming that event resumes or aborts — a clean round-trip.

全自动Fully automatic
快，但删错/下错单无法挽回
fast, but a wrong delete/order is irreversible
vs
关键步加闸Gate the risky step
仅高风险动作要人确认，其余自动
only high-risk actions need a human; the rest stays automatic
不是所有步都要人——只在不可逆/高风险处加闸not every step needs a human — gate only the irreversible/high-risk ones

① 为什么要人在回路：高风险 / 不可逆动作不能全自动① Why human-in-the-loop: high-risk / irreversible actions can't be fully automatic

L32 的小队越自由就越能干，但LLM 是概率的——它总有选错的时候。对大多数动作（读文档、起草文字、再查一次资料）来说，选错的代价很低：重试一次就好，没人受伤。可有一类动作会越过边界、落到真实世界：删库、转账、下单、对外发邮件 / 发消息——它们不可逆，一旦做错就收不回来，可能是真金白银的损失或对外的事故。正因如此，恰恰在这些点上不能让自主权独自拍板。HITL 的思路很简单：在不可逆的那一步前插入一个人，让人来做最后的批准。但人不是免费的——每一次确认都加延迟、打扰人，所以只把它放在代价最高、最不可逆的动作上；其余一切照常自动。这正是上一课结尾留下的那道“刹车”。
L32's team grows more capable as it grows freer, but an LLM is probabilistic — it will sometimes pick wrong. For most actions (reading a doc, drafting text, one more lookup) a wrong pick is cheap: just retry, no one gets hurt. But one class of action crosses the boundary into the real world: dropping a database, transferring money, placing an order, sending outbound email / messages — these are irreversible; once done wrong you can't take them back, and the loss can be real money or an outward-facing incident. That is exactly why, at those points, autonomy must not decide alone. HITL's idea is simple: insert a human right before the irreversible step and let them give the final approval. But a human isn't free — every confirmation adds latency and interrupts someone — so you reserve it for the costliest, least reversible actions and keep everything else automatic. This is the very “brake” the last lesson left off on.

② 机制：@step 返回 InputRequiredEvent 挂起，调用方回 HumanResponseEvent 恢复② Mechanism: a @step returns InputRequiredEvent to pause; the caller sends HumanResponseEvent to resume

承接 L32 的底层视角：agent 跑在 workflow 上，流程由 @step + 事件驱动。HITL 用的就是这套机器，只多了一对专门的事件，机制分两半、正好一来一回。① workflow 侧——挂起：某个 @step 在要动手前，把返回类型标成 InputRequiredEvent 并返回它。框架会自动把它写进事件流，而且不需要任何下游 step 去消费就能通过校验——于是流程停在这里、向人请求输入。InputRequiredEvent(prefix="…") 里的 prefix 就是要展示给人看的那句话（“确认要删账户吗？”）。② 调用方侧——回灌：发起 workflow 的人正用 async for ev in handler.stream_events() 盯着事件流；一旦看到 InputRequiredEvent，就拿 ev.prefix 去问真正的人（前端弹窗 / 审批系统 / 命令行），把人的回答装进 HumanResponseEvent(response=…)，用 handler.ctx.send_event(...) 送回 workflow。消费 HumanResponseEvent 的那个 @step 随即被唤醒，读 ev.response，据此恢复或中止。一句话：workflow 返回 InputRequiredEvent、调用方流式取到再送回 HumanResponseEvent，这“出—回”两步就是 HITL 的全部——prefix 把问题带出去，response 把人的决定带回来。
Continuing L32's under-the-hood view: an agent runs on a workflow, driven by @step + events. HITL uses that same machinery, plus one dedicated pair of events; the mechanism is two halves — exactly one round-trip. (1) Workflow side — pause: right before acting, a @step annotates its return as InputRequiredEvent and returns it. The framework auto-writes it to the event stream, and it needs no downstream step to consume it to pass validation — so the flow stops here and asks a human. The prefix in InputRequiredEvent(prefix="…") is the line to show the human (“confirm deleting the account?”). (2) Caller side — inject back: whoever launched the workflow is watching the stream with async for ev in handler.stream_events(); on seeing an InputRequiredEvent, it takes ev.prefix to ask a real human (a frontend dialog / approval system / CLI), wraps the answer in HumanResponseEvent(response=…), and sends it back with handler.ctx.send_event(...). The @step consuming HumanResponseEvent then wakes up, reads ev.response, and resumes or aborts accordingly. In a line: the workflow returns InputRequiredEvent, and the caller streams it and sends back HumanResponseEvent — that “out-and-back” pair is all of HITL: prefix carries the question out, response carries the human's decision back.
workflow 侧：act 这个 @step 返回 InputRequiredEvent——自动写入事件流并挂起；消费 HumanResponseEvent 的 finish 据 response 恢复或中止Workflow side: the act @step returns InputRequiredEvent — auto-written to the stream and pausing; finish, which consumes HumanResponseEvent, resumes or aborts on response
from llama_index.core.workflow import (Workflow, step, StartEvent, StopEvent,
                                        InputRequiredEvent, HumanResponseEvent)

class ApprovalFlow(Workflow):
    @step
    async def act(self, ev: StartEvent) -> InputRequiredEvent:
        return InputRequiredEvent(prefix="确认要执行『删除账户』吗？(yes/no) ")   # 写入事件流并挂起

    @step
    async def finish(self, ev: HumanResponseEvent) -> StopEvent:
        ok = ev.response.strip().lower() == "yes"
        return StopEvent(result="已执行" if ok else "已取消")
调用方侧：流式监听事件流，遇到 InputRequiredEvent 就拿 prefix 去问人，把答案装进 HumanResponseEvent 送回——await handler 取最终结果Caller side: stream the events; on InputRequiredEvent, use prefix to ask a human, wrap the answer in HumanResponseEvent and send it back — await handler for the result
handler = ApprovalFlow().run()
async for ev in handler.stream_events():
    if isinstance(ev, InputRequiredEvent):
        answer = input(ev.prefix)                              # 真实场景：来自前端/审批系统
        handler.ctx.send_event(HumanResponseEvent(response=answer))
result = await handler

人在回路：危险动作前暂停，拿到人的确认再继续HITL: pause before a risky action, resume only on human confirmation

③ 落点：审批闸、低置信度兜底、敏感工具调用前确认③ Where it lands: approval gates, low-confidence fallback, confirming before sensitive tool calls

HITL 在三处最常落地，但都遵循同一条线——只在该加闸的地方加闸。① 审批闸：在不可逆的对外动作前（删库 / 转账 / 下单 / 群发）强制一次人工 yes/no，就像上面的 ApprovalFlow——通过才执行，否则中止。② 低置信度兜底：当模型 / 检索没把握时（相似度过低、证据互相矛盾、模型自陈“不确定”），别硬编，转人工裁决；关键是设阈值——只有置信度低于线才弹给人，高置信的照常自动答，别让 HITL 变成“凡事都问”。③ 敏感工具调用前确认：给 agent 的工具分级——把 send_email / run_sql / place_order 标成“敏感”，agent 真要调用前暂停让人点头；而只读 / 可撤销的工具（检索、查天气）放它自己跑。三者都在解同一个问题：把极少数不可逆 / 高风险 / 低置信的点拦下来交给人，其余维持自动——这也正好接上 L25 的护栏（护栏自动挡掉明显违规，HITL 处理那些需要人判断的灰色地带）与 L23 的可观测（人要看得到上下文 / trace 才能拍好这一板）。
HITL lands in three common spots, all following one line — gate only where a gate belongs. (1) Approval gate: before an irreversible outward action (drop DB / transfer / order / mass-send), force a human yes/no, just like the ApprovalFlow above — execute on pass, abort otherwise. (2) Low-confidence fallback: when the model / retrieval is unsure (similarity too low, conflicting evidence, the model says “not sure”), don't fake it — escalate to a human; the key is a threshold: route to a human only below the line, answer high-confidence cases automatically, so HITL doesn't become “ask about everything”. (3) Confirm before sensitive tool calls: grade an agent's tools — mark send_email / run_sql / place_order as “sensitive” and pause for a human nod right before invoking them, while read-only / reversible tools (retrieval, weather) run on their own. All three solve the same problem: intercept the very few irreversible / high-risk / low-confidence points and hand them to a human, keeping the rest automatic — which dovetails with L25's guardrails (guardrails auto-block the obvious violations; HITL handles the gray zone that needs human judgment) and L23's observability (a human needs visible context / traces to make the call well).
🧩 生活类比🧩 Analogy
HITL 像网银支付前的“二次确认弹窗”：你平时查余额、看账单都畅通无阻，可一旦要真把钱转出去，屏幕就弹一个框——“确认向 ××× 转账 ¥5000？”——停在这里等你按下确认，你点了才扣款、取消就作罢。它不挡大多数操作，只在那一步不可逆的关键动作上拦一下，把最终决定权交回给你。
HITL is like the “confirm” dialog before an online-banking payment: browsing your balance or statements flows freely, but the moment you actually move money out, a box pops up — “Confirm transferring ¥5000 to ×××?” — and it waits for you to press confirm; only then does it debit, and cancel calls it off. It blocks almost nothing, stepping in only at that one irreversible, critical action, handing the final decision back to you.
✅ 本课要点✅ Key points
  • HITL 是给不可逆 / 高风险动作（删库、转账、下单、外发）装的刹车：动手前暂停、等人确认——但只在该加闸的那一步加，不是每步都要人。HITL is a brake for irreversible / high-risk actions (drop DB, transfer, order, outbound): pause before acting and wait for a human — but gate only that step, not every step.
  • 机制是一对事件的来回：一个 @step 返回 InputRequiredEvent（自动写入事件流、挂起）；调用方流式取到后回一个 HumanResponseEvent，消费它的 @step 据 response 恢复 / 中止（prefix 带问题出去）。The mechanism is one round-trip of a pair of events: a @step returns InputRequiredEvent (auto-written to the stream, pausing); the caller streams it and sends back a HumanResponseEvent, and the consuming @step resumes / aborts on response (prefix carries the question out).
  • 三个落点：审批闸（不可逆外部动作前）、低置信度兜底（分数过低 / 证据矛盾时转人）、敏感工具调用前确认（给工具分级，只对敏感的暂停）。Three landing spots: an approval gate (before irreversible external actions), a low-confidence fallback (escalate when scores are low / evidence conflicts), and confirming before sensitive tool calls (grade tools, pause only for sensitive ones).
  • 人是最贵的一层：每次确认都加延迟、打扰人——所以触发要省着用，并与 L25 护栏 + L23 trace 叠成三层纵深（机器能判的别劳烦人，人判时要有上下文）。A human is the most expensive layer: each confirm adds latency and interruption — so trigger it sparingly, and stack it with L25 guardrails + L23 traces into three-layer defense in depth (don't bother a human with what a machine can judge; give context when a human does).
💡 设计亮点💡 Design insight
人在回路的精髓，不是“让人盯着每一步”，而是把人放在最该放的那一个点上。L32 给了我们一支自由、能干的小队，可自由一旦延伸到不可逆的边界——删库、转账、外发——就危险了；HITL 就是那道刹车。但真正的设计判断不在“要不要人”，而在“在哪一步要人”：只在不可逆 / 高风险 / 低置信的极少数点上暂停，其余全自动——闸加错地方，要么拦不住事故，要么把吞吐拖垮、把人烦走。把它放进全书的脉络看，这是三层纵深的最后一层：L25 护栏自动挡掉明显违规（机器能判的，别劳烦人），L23 可观测把上下文 / trace 摆到人面前（让这一板拍得有依据），L33 HITL 在闸口让人做最后的拍板。人是最贵也最后的一层，所以只用在代价最高、最不可逆的地方。机制上它又轻得恰到好处：一个 @step 返回 InputRequiredEvent 就挂起、调用方回一个 HumanResponseEvent 就恢复——安全不是关掉自主，而是在关键一步把决定权短暂交回给人。下一课 L34，我们就把这套带着刹车的系统真正上线成服务。
The essence of human-in-the-loop isn't “make a human watch every step” but placing the human at the one point that matters most. L32 handed us a free, capable team, but once that freedom reaches an irreversible boundary — dropping a DB, transferring money, sending outbound — it turns dangerous; HITL is that brake. Yet the real design call isn't “human or not” but “at which step”: pause only at the very few irreversible / high-risk / low-confidence points and keep the rest automatic — gate the wrong place and you either fail to stop the incident or grind throughput and annoy the human away. Seen across the whole book, this is the last of three layers of defense in depth: L25 guardrails auto-block the obvious violations (don't bother a human with what a machine can judge), L23 observability puts context / traces in front of the human (so the call is well-grounded), and L33 HITL lets a human make the final decision at the gate. The human is the most expensive, last layer, so spend it only where the downside is costliest and least reversible. And the mechanism stays just light enough: a @step returning InputRequiredEvent pauses, a caller's HumanResponseEvent resumes — safety isn't switching off autonomy but briefly handing the decision back to a human at the critical step. Next, L34 takes this brake-equipped system and actually ships it as a service.

🧪 自测 · 想一想为什么这么设计🧪 Self-check · think about the design

1. 在 LlamaIndex workflow 里，HITL（暂停等人确认）靠什么实现？In a LlamaIndex workflow, what implements HITL (pausing for a human's confirmation)?
  1. 一个 @step 返回 InputRequiredEvent 挂起、调用方回 HumanResponseEvent 恢复a @step returns InputRequiredEvent to pause; the caller sends back HumanResponseEvent to resume
  2. 用 rerank 重排候选re-rank candidates with a reranker
  3. 关闭 LLM 调用disable the LLM call
  4. 打开流式逐字输出turn on token-by-token streaming
看答案与解析Show answer & explanation 点击展开expand
答案：AAnswer: A HITL 的机制就是这一对事件：某个 @step 返回 InputRequiredEvent——它被自动写入事件流、无需下游消费即挂起流程；调用方从流里取到后，回一个 HumanResponseEvent(response=…)，消费它的 @step 据此恢复或中止。“关闭 LLM 调用”只是不用模型、与“暂停等人”无关；“用 rerank 重排候选”是检索后处理（L13）、改的是结果顺序；“打开流式逐字输出”只是把答案一个字一个字地吐出来、是展示方式——三者都不会让流程停下来等人点头。HITL's mechanism is exactly this pair of events: a @step returns an InputRequiredEvent — auto-written to the event stream and pausing the flow with no downstream consumer; the caller picks it up from the stream and sends back a HumanResponseEvent(response=…), and the @step consuming it resumes or aborts. “Disabling the LLM call” just means not using the model — nothing to do with “pause for a human”; “re-ranking candidates with a reranker” is retrieval post-processing (L13) that reorders results; “turning on token-by-token streaming” merely emits the answer one token at a time, a display choice — none of the three stops the flow to wait for a human nod.

🎯 面试官提问 · 试着答出要点🎯 Interviewer asks · cover the key points

🎯 1. 你给 agent 加了 HITL 后，QA 抱怨“太慢、老被弹窗打断”。在不牺牲安全的前提下，你怎么把对人的打扰降到最低？After you added HITL, QA complains it's “too slow, constantly interrupted by confirm dialogs”. Without sacrificing safety, how do you cut the interruption to a human to a minimum?
看参考要点Show key points 点击展开expand
🔑 重点：HITL 的成本来自“弹窗的频率”，所以核心是少弹、晚弹、聪明地弹——只在不可逆 / 高风险 / 低置信处触发，能批量就批量，并给默认超时与回退，别让流程死等人。① 收窄触发面：只给真正不可逆 / 高风险的动作（删库、转账、外发）和低置信（分数过低、证据矛盾）加闸；只读 / 可撤销的操作一律自动，别“凡事都问”。② 批量确认：把一段时间内的多个待批聚成一屏让人一次点完，而不是一个动作弹一次——既省打扰又省上下文切换。③ 设默认与超时：给每个确认配超时 + 默认策略（高风险默认“拒”、低风险默认“放”），人没在 N 分钟内回就走默认，绝不无限期挂起。④ 上下文一次给足：弹窗里把 prefix 写清楚（要做什么、影响什么、依据是什么，呼应 L23 的 trace），让人一眼能判，减少来回追问。⑤ 事后调阈值：统计确认通过率——某类动作若人几乎总点“yes”，说明这道闸加得过密，可以放宽或撤掉。🔑 Key: HITL's cost comes from “how often it pops up”, so the core is to pop up less, later, and smarter — trigger only at irreversible / high-risk / low-confidence points, batch when you can, and give defaults plus timeouts so the flow never dead-waits on a human. (1) Narrow the trigger surface: gate only truly irreversible / high-risk actions (drop DB, transfer, outbound) and low-confidence cases (score too low, conflicting evidence); auto-run read-only / reversible ops — don't “ask about everything”. (2) Batch confirmations: collect several pending approvals over a window into one screen to clear at once, instead of one popup per action — saving both interruption and context-switching. (3) Defaults and timeouts: pair each confirm with a timeout + default policy (high-risk defaults to “deny”, low-risk to “allow”); if no reply within N minutes, take the default and never hang indefinitely. (4) Give full context once: write a clear prefix (what it will do, what it affects, on what basis — echoing L23's traces) so the human can judge at a glance, cutting back-and-forth. (5) Tune thresholds afterward: track the approval rate — if a class of action is almost always “yes”, that gate is too dense and can be loosened or removed.
🎯 2. HITL 和你前面做的护栏（L25）、可观测（L23）是什么关系？它们是重复造轮子，还是各司其职？How does HITL relate to the guardrails (L25) and observability (L23) you built earlier? Are they redundant, or does each play its own role?
看参考要点Show key points 点击展开expand
🔑 重点：三者不是重复，而是三层纵深防御——护栏自动挡掉明显违规，trace 让人看清上下文，HITL 是最后那道“人来拍板”的闸；越往后越贵，所以越往后用得越省。① L25 护栏：自动、廉价、挡明显的。规则 / 分类器能判定的（注入、越权、明显有害）就直接拒，根本不该惊动人——机器能判的别劳烦人。② L23 可观测：让决定有依据。当事情落到人手里，人得看到这一步要做什么、基于哪些证据、前面怎么走过来的——trace / 上下文就是人做判断的仪表盘，没有它人只能瞎点。③ L33 HITL：灰色地带的最终裁决。规则判不了、又不可逆 / 高风险的，才交给人点头——这是最贵的一层（要人、要等），所以放在最后、用得最省。④ 一句话：护栏管“明显该拦的”，HITL 管“该不该做得让人判的”，可观测让这两件事都看得见、查得到——三层叠起来才既安全又不拖垮效率。🔑 Key: the three aren't redundant but three layers of defense in depth — guardrails auto-block obvious violations, traces let a human see the context, and HITL is the final “human decides” gate; each later layer is pricier, so each is used more sparingly. (1) L25 guardrails: automatic, cheap, catch the obvious. What a rule / classifier can judge (injection, over-reach, plainly harmful) is rejected outright and should never reach a human — don't bother a person with what a machine can decide. (2) L23 observability: ground the decision. When something does fall to a human, they need to see what this step will do, on what evidence, and how it got here — traces / context are the human's dashboard; without it they're just guessing. (3) L33 HITL: final ruling for the gray zone. Only the irreversible / high-risk cases a rule can't settle go to a human nod — the most expensive layer (needs a person, needs waiting), so it sits last and is used most sparingly. (4) In a line: guardrails handle “the obviously blockable”, HITL handles “whether-to-do that needs human judgment”, and observability makes both visible and auditable — stacked, the three are safe without grinding down efficiency.
第 1 层 · 护栏 (L25)Layer 1 · Guardrails (L25)自动挡掉明显违规——机器能判的不劳人auto-block obvious violations — no human for what a machine can judge
第 2 层 · 可观测 (L23)Layer 2 · Observability (L23)把上下文 / trace 摆到人面前，让拍板有依据put context / traces before the human so the call is grounded
第 3 层 · HITL (L33)Layer 3 · HITL (L33)闸口由人做最后拍板——最贵也最后的一层a human makes the final call at the gate — the last, most expensive layer
三层纵深：护栏自动挡、trace 让人看清、HITL 最后由人拍板Defense in depth: guardrails auto-block, traces clarify, HITL leaves the final call to a human
🎯 3. 现实里人可能几小时甚至隔天才点确认，可你的进程不能一直挂着干等。你怎么设计让 workflow 能挂起、等很久、再恢复？In reality a human may take hours or even a day to confirm, but your process can't sit there blocking. How do you design the workflow to pause, wait a long time, then resume?
看参考要点Show key points 点击展开expand
🔑 重点：把“等人”做成异步 + 可持久化——发出 InputRequiredEvent 后序列化 workflow 的上下文（Context）落库，进程可以释放；人回来时再从存档恢复、灌入 HumanResponseEvent 续跑，而不是让线程死等。① 别阻塞等待：挂起点不该占着进程 / 线程空转。拿到 InputRequiredEvent 就把待批请求 + 上下文快照存起来（ctx.to_dict() 落 DB / 队列），释放资源。② 持久化状态：workflow 的 Context 可序列化——这正是“等很久”的关键：状态在库里而不在内存里，进程重启 / 扩缩容都不丢。③ 回来再恢复：人在前端 / 审批系统点了确认，后端用存档重建 Context（Context.from_dict），send_event(HumanResponseEvent(response=…)) 让消费它的 step 续跑。④ 配套要有超时与对账：长时间没人理要能超时走默认或提醒重派，并保证“同一请求只批一次”（幂等），别因为重试把高风险动作执行两遍。🔑 Key: make “waiting on a human” async + persistable — after emitting InputRequiredEvent, serialize the workflow's Context to storage and let the process go; when the human returns, restore from that snapshot and inject the HumanResponseEvent to continue, rather than blocking a thread. (1) Don't block-wait: a pause point shouldn't hold a process / thread spinning. On InputRequiredEvent, persist the pending request + a context snapshot (ctx.to_dict() to DB / queue) and release resources. (2) Persist the state: the workflow's Context is serializable — exactly what makes “wait a long time” possible: state lives in storage, not memory, so restarts / autoscaling don't lose it. (3) Resume on return: when the human confirms in a frontend / approval system, the backend rebuilds the Context from the snapshot (Context.from_dict) and send_event(HumanResponseEvent(response=…)) lets the consuming step continue. (4) Pair it with timeouts and reconciliation: a long-unanswered request must time out to a default or nudge / reassign, and guarantee “each request is approved once” (idempotent) so a retry doesn't execute a high-risk action twice.
💭 发散思考（没有标准答案）💭 Open questions (no single right answer)
  • 哪些动作该加人工确认、哪些不该？（提示：不可逆 / 高风险——删除 / 转账 / 外发——该加闸；只读 / 可撤销 / 低风险——检索 / 起草 / 计算——放行；别让 HITL 把吞吐拖垮、把人烦走）Which actions should get a human confirm and which shouldn't? (Hint: irreversible / high-risk — delete / transfer / outbound — gate them; read-only / reversible / low-risk — retrieve / draft / compute — let them through; don't let HITL grind throughput or annoy the human away)
第八部分 · Agentic 进阶与上线

34 · 上线服务

写入路径Write path加载Load切块SplitEmbedEmbed存储Store索引Index
查询路径Query path检索Retrieve后处理Post-process合成Synthesize回答Answer

前面 33 课，我们的 RAG 一直活在 notebook 里：建一次索引、问几个问题、看看效果——能跑一次就算赢。可真正交付时，它得变成一个 7×24 营业的服务：通过 HTTP 同时接很多人的请求、要稳、要快。从原型到服务，最该避免的一件事就是——每来一个请求就重新加载 / 重建索引。建库（读文件、切块、embedding、写库）是一次性的重活，把它摊进每一次查询，结果就是又慢又浪费、并发一上来就垮。正解只有一句：索引在启动时一次加载、常驻内存，查询引擎复用，每个请求只跑「检索+合成」这段轻活。这一课就把这条规则落地：① 用 FastAPI 把常驻的查询引擎包成一个 HTTP 接口，配 async aquery / 流式扛并发、降首 token 延迟（承 L24）；② 用 persist / load_index_from_storage 让服务启动即秒级恢复、不必每次重建（承 L11）；③ 再往上，llama-deploy 编排多 workflow/服务、create-llama 脚手架快速起项目。说明：FastAPI / llama-deploy / create-llama 都在 core 之外，本课代码是示例；真正的 core 只有你早就会的 StorageContext / load_index_from_storage / as_query_engine / aquery。For 33 lessons our RAG has lived in a notebook: build the index once, ask a few questions, eyeball the result — running once is a win. But to actually ship it, it must become a 24/7 service: taking many people's requests over HTTP at once, staying stable and fast. Going from prototype to service, the one thing to avoid most is reloading / rebuilding the index on every request. Building the library (read files, chunk, embed, write the store) is a one-time heavy job; smear it across every query and you get slow, wasteful work that collapses under concurrency. The fix is one sentence: load the index once at startup, keep it resident in memory, and reuse the query engine, so each request runs only the light “retrieve + synthesize” part. This lesson makes that rule concrete: (1) use FastAPI to wrap the resident query engine as an HTTP endpoint, with async aquery / streaming to handle concurrency and cut first-token latency (from L24); (2) use persist / load_index_from_storage so the service restores in seconds at startup instead of rebuilding every time (from L11); (3) one level up, llama-deploy orchestrates multiple workflows/services and create-llama scaffolds a project fast. Note: FastAPI / llama-deploy / create-llama all live outside core; the code here is illustrative; the real core is only what you already know — StorageContext / load_index_from_storage / as_query_engine / aquery.

每请求重建索引Rebuild per request
每来一个请求就 load / 重建一次——把一次性建库成本摊进每次查询，又慢又浪费，并发一上来就垮。
every request does a load / rebuild — smearing the one-time build cost into each query: slow, wasteful, and collapses under concurrency.
vs
启动一次、引擎常驻Load once, engine resident
启动时一次加载索引、查询引擎常驻复用，每个请求只跑「检索+合成」——快、省、扛并发。
load the index once at startup and reuse the resident query engine; each request runs only “retrieve + synthesize” — fast, cheap, concurrency-ready.
上线第一课：把建库成本留在启动，别摊进每次请求Serving rule #1: keep the build cost at startup, don't smear it into every request

① 从 notebook 到服务：索引一次加载常驻，别每请求重建① From notebook to service: load the index once and keep it resident — don't rebuild per request

notebook 和服务，活法完全不同。在 notebook 里，你从上往下跑一遍：建索引那个 cell 只执行一次，之后的 query 都复用内存里那个 index——跑通一次就够了。可服务是长命的、并发的：它常驻进程、通过 HTTP 同时接很多请求，一天跑几万次。这时一个在 notebook 里看不出问题的写法会变成致命伤——把建索引写进请求处理函数里。建库是读文件 → 切块 → embedding → 写向量库这一整套重活，慢、烧钱、只需做一次；可一旦它躺在每个请求的代码路径上，就等于每问一个问题都把整个图书馆重建一遍——延迟高到没法用，embedding 费用成倍涨，并发稍一上来内存和算力就被重复建库吃垮。解法是把「建一次」和「查很多次」彻底分开：在服务启动时（模块加载 / app 启动）一次性把索引加载进内存，得到一个常驻的查询引擎；之后每个请求只调用这个已存在的引擎，跑「检索 + 合成」这段轻活。一句话——重活留在启动，请求里只剩轻活。这条规则贯穿后面三节：异步让「轻活」并发跑得更稳（②），持久化让「启动加载」便宜到秒级（③），编排让多个这样的服务协同（④）。
A notebook and a service live completely differently. In a notebook you run top to bottom: the cell that builds the index runs once, and later query calls reuse that in-memory index — running it once is enough. A service is long-lived and concurrent: it sits resident in a process, takes many requests over HTTP at once, tens of thousands a day. Here a pattern that looks harmless in a notebook turns fatal — building the index inside the request handler. Building the library is the whole heavy chain of read files → chunk → embed → write the vector store: slow, costly, and needed only once; put it on every request's code path and you rebuild the entire library for every single question — latency too high to use, embedding bills multiplying, and memory/compute crushed by repeated rebuilds the moment concurrency rises. The fix is to fully separate “build once” from “query many times”: at service startup (module load / app startup) load the index into memory once, yielding a resident query engine; then each request calls that already-existing engine to run the light “retrieve + synthesize” part. In a line — keep the heavy work at startup, leave only light work in the request. This rule runs through the next three sections: async makes the “light work” run concurrently and stably (②), persistence makes “startup loading” cheap down to seconds (③), and orchestration lets many such services cooperate (④).
示例服务：模块级一次 load_index_from_storage 常驻、引擎复用；请求里只 await aquery（FastAPI 在 core 之外）Illustrative service: module-level load_index_from_storage once and resident, engine reused; the request only awaits aquery (FastAPI is outside core)
# pip install fastapi uvicorn  —— 以下为示例，FastAPI/llama-deploy 在 core 之外
from fastapi import FastAPI
from llama_index.core import StorageContext, load_index_from_storage

app = FastAPI()
index = load_index_from_storage(StorageContext.from_defaults(persist_dir="./store"))  # 启动时一次加载
qe = index.as_query_engine()

@app.post("/query")
async def query(q: str):
    return {"answer": str(await qe.aquery(q))}   # 异步，承 L24
🔬 源码对应🔬 In the source
indices/loading.py · load_index_from_storage — 从磁盘恢复已建好的索引，服务启动时一次加载常驻。restores a persisted index from disk — loaded once at service startup.
HTTP 请求HTTP requestFastAPI 路由FastAPI route
常驻查询引擎long-lived query engine启动时一次加载索引index loaded once at boot
检索 + 合成retrieve + synthesize异步/流式async/streaming
LLMLLM生成答案generates answer
上线关键：索引常驻、查询引擎复用，别每请求重建serving rule: keep the index resident and reuse the engine — don't rebuild per request

② 用 FastAPI 把查询引擎包成接口：async aquery / 流式扛并发（承 L24）② Wrap the query engine as an endpoint with FastAPI: async aquery / streaming for concurrency (from L24)

有了常驻的查询引擎，剩下的只是「把它接到网上」。FastAPI（pip install fastapi uvicorn，core 之外的 Web 框架，本课只作示例）正合适：它原生 async，和我们 L24 学的 aquery 天生一对。为什么要 async？因为 RAG 的一次查询，大半时间卡在等 LLM / 等向量库返回——这是 I/O 等待，不是 CPU 在算。同步的 query 会把整个进程堵死在这一次等待上，后面排队的请求只能干等；而 async def + await qe.aquery(q) 在等待时把控制权交还事件循环，让别的请求继续跑——同样一台机器，并发吞吐立刻上一个台阶（承 L24 的「异步/批」）。另一半是体验：用流式（承 L24）让答案逐 token 边生成边吐，用户几百毫秒就看到第一个字，而不是干等整段生成完——首 token 延迟骤降，总时长几乎不变。要记牢 L24 的那句话：流式优化的是「首字延迟」与体验，不是总耗时。分清边界：aquery 是core 的真方法（它能直接收一个字符串问题）；FastAPI / uvicorn 是外部工具，只是把这个 core 能力暴露成 HTTP。
With a resident query engine, all that's left is “wiring it to the network”. FastAPI (pip install fastapi uvicorn, a Web framework outside core, illustrative here) fits well: it is natively async and a natural match for the aquery we learned in L24. Why async? Because most of a RAG query's time is spent waiting on the LLM / the vector store — that's I/O wait, not CPU work. A synchronous query blocks the whole process on that one wait, so queued requests just sit idle; whereas async def + await qe.aquery(q) yields control back to the event loop while waiting, letting other requests keep running — on the same machine, concurrent throughput jumps a level (L24's “async / batch”). The other half is experience: streaming (from L24) emits the answer token by token as it generates, so the user sees the first character in a few hundred milliseconds instead of waiting for the whole thing — first-token latency drops sharply while total time barely changes. Remember L24's line: streaming optimizes “first-token latency” and experience, not total time. Keep the boundary clear: aquery is a real core method (it takes a string question directly); FastAPI / uvicorn are external tools that merely expose that core capability over HTTP.

③ 持久化：persist / load_index_from_storage 让启动即秒级恢复（承 L11）③ Persistence: persist / load_index_from_storage for second-level startup recovery (from L11)

「启动时一次加载」要真便宜，前提是别在启动时也重建一遍。如果每次服务启动都从原始文档重新切块、重新 embedding，那「建库的重活」只是从「每请求」挪到了「每次重启 / 每次扩容」——部署一次等几分钟、还白烧 embedding 钱。L11 的持久化正是为此：建一次、落一次盘——index.storage_context.persist(persist_dir="./store") 把 docstore / index / 向量整套写到磁盘；之后服务启动只需 load_index_from_storage(StorageContext.from_defaults(persist_dir="./store"))，秒级把索引读回内存，免去重建。这正是上面 code① 启动那一行在做的事。这两个符号都是实打实的 core（StorageContext 来自 storage_context.py、load_index_from_storage 来自 indices/loading.py），不依赖任何外部框架。再往规模化看一步：当你跑多个副本（多进程 / 多机水平扩展）时，别让每个副本各存一份本地索引，而是让它们共享同一份持久化存储，或干脆把向量接到外置向量库（L09 学过的 Chroma / pgvector / Qdrant…）——这样「加载一次」对每个副本都成立，数据也只有一处真相。
For “load once at startup” to be truly cheap, you must not rebuild at startup either. If every service start re-chunks and re-embeds from the raw documents, the “build heavy lifting” has merely moved from “per request” to “per restart / per scale-out” — minutes of wait per deploy and wasted embedding spend. L11's persistence exists for this: build once, write once — index.storage_context.persist(persist_dir="./store") writes the docstore / index / vectors to disk; afterward a service start only needs load_index_from_storage(StorageContext.from_defaults(persist_dir="./store")) to read the index back into memory in seconds, skipping the rebuild. This is exactly what the startup line in code① above does. Both symbols are genuine core (StorageContext from storage_context.py, load_index_from_storage from indices/loading.py), depending on no external framework. One step toward scale: when you run multiple replicas (multi-process / multi-machine horizontal scaling), don't let each replica keep its own local copy — have them share one persisted store, or connect vectors to an external vector DB (the Chroma / pgvector / Qdrant… from L09) — so “load once” holds for every replica and the data has a single source of truth.

④ 更进一步：llama-deploy 编排多 workflow/服务、create-llama 脚手架起项目④ Going further: llama-deploy orchestrates multi-workflow services, create-llama scaffolds a project

一个 FastAPI 文件足够把单个查询引擎送上线；但当系统长大——L32 的多 agent / 多 workflow、L33 的 HITL 审批都要协同时，你会想要编排而不是手搓。这里有两件 core 之外的官方工具（同样只作示例）：① llama-deploy——把你写好的 workflow 部署成可独立伸缩、能互相通信的网络服务，多个 workflow/服务由它统一编排、扩缩容，等于把 L26–L33 搭的那套从「一个进程里的对象」升级成「一组分布式服务」。② create-llama——一个脚手架 CLI（npx create-llama），一条命令生成前端 + 后端 + 数据摄取的全栈起手项目，省去你手搓 API、UI、ingestion 的样板，几分钟就能跑起一个能问答的网站。务必记住边界：llama-deploy / create-llama / FastAPI 都不是 core，它们是打包与编排层；真正干活的核心始终没变——还是你早已会的索引、查询引擎、workflow。怎么选：起步 / 单服务，FastAPI 足矣；要从零快速起一个全栈项目，用 create-llama 脚手架；要把多个 workflow/服务编排成分布式系统，再上 llama-deploy。
A single FastAPI file is enough to ship one query engine; but as the system grows — L32's multi-agent / multi-workflow and L33's HITL approvals all need to cooperate — you'll want orchestration rather than hand-wiring. Here are two out-of-core official tools (again illustrative only): (1) llama-deploy — deploys the workflows you wrote as independently scalable, mutually communicating networked services, orchestrating and autoscaling many workflows/services, effectively upgrading the L26–L33 stack from “objects in one process” to “a set of distributed services”. (2) create-llama — a scaffold CLI (npx create-llama) that generates a full-stack starter with frontend + backend + ingestion in one command, sparing you the boilerplate of hand-building API, UI, and ingestion, so a working Q&A site runs in minutes. Keep the boundary firmly in mind: llama-deploy / create-llama / FastAPI are not core — they are a packaging and orchestration layer; the core that does the real work never changed — still the index, query engine, and workflow you already know. How to choose: for a start / single service, FastAPI is enough; to spin up a full-stack project from scratch fast, use the create-llama scaffold; to orchestrate many workflows/services into a distributed system, reach for llama-deploy.
notebook 原型notebook prototype
→
FastAPI 服务FastAPI service
并发/流式concurrent/streaming
→
llama-deploy / create-llamallama-deploy / create-llama
编排/脚手架orchestration/scaffold
从原型到生产服务的进阶路径the path from prototype to a production service
🧩 生活类比🧩 Analogy
把 RAG 上线，就像把实验台上的原型搬进一家7×24 营业的店面。在实验台上，原型能点亮一次就算成功——你亲手接线、跑一遍、记下结果。可开门做生意完全是另一回事：店面要常年不打烊、要同时接待很多客人、上菜要快。于是你不会每来一位客人就重盖一次厨房（那就是「每请求重建索引」）——厨房开业前就装好、一直备着（索引常驻），客人来了只管下单上菜（检索+合成）；还得能同时招呼多桌（async 并发）、先端上一道前菜稳住客人（流式降首字延迟）；打烊重开也不必重装厨房（持久化）。原型只要能跑一次，店面要稳、要快、要能同时接客——这一步之差，就是 notebook 与服务的全部距离。
Shipping a RAG is like moving a prototype off the lab bench into a shop open 24/7. On the bench, lighting the prototype up once is success — you wire it by hand, run it through, note the result. Opening for business is another matter entirely: the shop must never close, serve many customers at once, and bring food out fast. So you don't rebuild the kitchen for every customer who walks in (that's “rebuild the index per request”) — the kitchen is installed before opening and kept ready (a resident index), and each guest just orders and is served (retrieve + synthesize); you also wait many tables at once (async concurrency) and bring out a starter first to settle them (streaming cuts first-token latency); closing and reopening needn't reinstall the kitchen (persistence). A prototype only has to run once; a shop has to be stable, fast, and able to serve many at once — that gap is the whole distance between a notebook and a service.
✅ 本课要点✅ Key points
  • 索引常驻、引擎复用，别每请求重建：建库（读文件 / 切块 / embedding / 写库）是一次性重活，摊进每次查询就又慢又浪费——启动时一次 load_index_from_storage 加载、查询引擎常驻，请求里只跑「检索+合成」。Keep the index resident, reuse the engine, don't rebuild per request: building the library (read files / chunk / embed / write) is one-time heavy work, and smearing it across every query is slow and wasteful — load once at startup with load_index_from_storage, keep the query engine resident, and run only “retrieve + synthesize” in the request.
  • FastAPI 只是示例 Web 框架（core 之外）：用 async def + await qe.aquery(q) 扛并发、用流式降首 token 延迟（都承 L24）；真正的 core 是查询引擎与 aquery，FastAPI 只是把它暴露成 HTTP。FastAPI is just an illustrative Web framework (outside core): use async def + await qe.aquery(q) for concurrency and streaming to cut first-token latency (both from L24); the real core is the query engine and aquery, FastAPI only exposes it over HTTP.
  • 持久化让「启动即恢复」便宜：persist 落盘、load_index_from_storage 秒级读回（承 L11），别在每次重启 / 扩容时重建；多副本应共享同一存储 / 外置向量库。Persistence makes “restore at startup” cheap: persist to disk and load_index_from_storage back in seconds (from L11), don't rebuild on every restart / scale-out; replicas should share one store / an external vector DB.
  • 再进一步是编排，不是新核心：llama-deploy 把多 workflow/服务编排成分布式系统、create-llama 脚手架快速起全栈项目——都在 core 之外、代码为示例。The next step is orchestration, not a new core: llama-deploy orchestrates multi-workflow services into a distributed system, create-llama scaffolds a full-stack project fast — both outside core, illustrative code.
  • 分清 core 与外部工具：StorageContext / load_index_from_storage / as_query_engine / aquery 是 core；FastAPI / llama-deploy / create-llama 是外部工具，按需取用、别当核心内置。Tell core from external tools: StorageContext / load_index_from_storage / as_query_engine / aquery are core; FastAPI / llama-deploy / create-llama are external tools — use on demand, don't mistake them for core built-ins.
💡 设计亮点💡 Design insight
上线这一课，几乎没有新的 RAG 概念——它的全部重量压在一句运维直觉上：把一次性的重活留在启动，把高频的轻活留在请求。索引常驻、查询引擎复用，别每请求重建——这就是 notebook 与服务之间唯一却致命的那道坎。想清楚这一点，剩下的拼图你早就备齐了：L24 的 async aquery + 流式解决「同时接客」与「首字延迟」，L11 的 persist / load 让「启动即恢复」便宜到秒级；FastAPI 只是把这套 core 能力接到网上的一层皮，llama-deploy / create-llama 则在更高处编排与脚手架——它们都在 core 之外，核心始终是你从第 1 课搭到第 33 课的那条 RAG 管线。而「上线」从来不是终点：服务跑起来之后，质量靠全书攒下的那套纵深持续兜住——L22 回归闸在每次发布前挡住退化，L23 trace 在出错时定位是检索还漏在生成，L25 护栏自动挡掉明显违规，必要时再用 L33 HITL 在不可逆的关口让人拍板。一句话收束：上线不是写新魔法，而是把你已经会的东西，按「常驻 + 异步 + 持久化」的纪律稳稳地摆上货架。
This shipping lesson brings almost no new RAG concept — its whole weight rests on one ops instinct: keep the one-time heavy work at startup and the high-frequency light work in the request. Keep the index resident, reuse the query engine, don't rebuild per request — that is the single, fatal step between a notebook and a service. Get that, and the rest of the puzzle you already have: L24's async aquery + streaming handles “serving many at once” and “first-token latency”, and L11's persist / load makes “restore at startup” cheap down to seconds; FastAPI is just a skin that wires this core capability to the network, while llama-deploy / create-llama orchestrate and scaffold one level up — all outside core, the core still being the RAG pipeline you built from L1 through L33. And “going live” is never the finish line: once the service runs, quality is held up by the defense in depth the whole book accumulated — L22's regression gate blocks regressions before each release, L23's traces localize whether a miss was in retrieval or generation, L25's guardrails auto-block obvious violations, and L33's HITL hands the call to a human at irreversible gates when needed. To close in a line: shipping isn't writing new magic — it's placing what you already know on the shelf, steadily, under the discipline of “resident + async + persistent”.

🧪 自测 · 想一想为什么这么设计🧪 Self-check · think about the design

1. 把 RAG 上线成服务，最该避免的做法是？When shipping a RAG as a service, which practice should you most avoid?
  1. 用 aquery 异步处理并发use aquery to handle concurrency asynchronously
  2. 每个请求都重新加载 / 重建索引reload / rebuild the index on every request
  3. 把索引持久化到磁盘persist the index to disk
  4. 启动时加载一次、查询引擎常驻复用load once at startup and reuse a resident query engine
看答案与解析Show answer & explanation 点击展开expand
答案：BAnswer: B 题目问的是「最该避免」。每个请求都重新加载 / 重建索引会把一次性建库成本（读文件 / 切块 / embedding / 写库）摊到每一次查询上——又慢又浪费，并发一上来就垮，正是上线第一大忌。其余三项恰恰都是该做的正解：「启动时加载一次、查询引擎常驻复用」把重活留在启动、请求里只剩轻活；「用 aquery 异步处理并发」在等 LLM / 向量库时让别的请求继续跑（承 L24）；「把索引持久化到磁盘」让启动用 load_index_from_storage 秒级恢复、免去重建（承 L11）。The question asks what to most avoid. Reloading / rebuilding the index on every request smears the one-time build cost (read files / chunk / embed / write) across every single query — slow, wasteful, and collapsing under concurrency: the cardinal serving sin. The other three are exactly the right things to do: “load once at startup and reuse a resident query engine” keeps the heavy work at startup and leaves only light work in the request; “use aquery to handle concurrency” lets other requests run while waiting on the LLM / vector store (from L24); and “persist the index to disk” lets startup restore in seconds via load_index_from_storage instead of rebuilding (from L11).

🎯 面试官提问 · 试着答出要点🎯 Interviewer asks · cover the key points

🎯 1. 你把 L20 的 capstone RAG 包成 FastAPI 服务上线，压测时发现：QPS 一高就雪崩，而且每次重启都要等好几分钟才能接客。你会怎么定位并优化并发与冷启动？You wrapped the L20 capstone RAG into a FastAPI service; under load testing you find it avalanches as QPS rises and every restart takes minutes before it can serve. How would you diagnose and optimize concurrency and cold start?
看参考要点Show key points 点击展开expand
🔑 重点：先把「建一次」和「查很多次」彻底分开——索引常驻、只在启动加载一次；再让请求路径全异步、把外部连接池化复用、启动时预热，并用限流给峰值兜底。① 查雪崩的根因：十有八九是把建索引 / 加载写进了请求处理函数——每个请求都重切块、重 embedding，CPU 和内存被重复建库吃垮。把它提到模块级 / 启动钩子，全局只 load_index_from_storage 一次、查询引擎常驻复用。② 请求路径全异步：用 async def + await qe.aquery(q)（承 L24），别在 async 视图里夹同步阻塞调用，否则照样堵死事件循环。③ 连接池 / 复用：向量库、LLM 客户端都用连接池，别每请求新建连接；embedding / LLM 尽量批量。④ 治冷启动：靠持久化（承 L11）让启动 load 是秒级而非重建；启动后预热——先打一条假查询，把模型 / 缓存 / 连接热起来再挂上健康检查（readiness）接流量。⑤ 限流 + 超时：给并发设上限、给慢请求设超时，峰值时排队或拒绝而不是拖垮整机；配合水平扩容多副本共享同一份持久化存储。最后用 L23 的 trace 确认瓶颈到底在检索、LLM 还是 I/O 等待。🔑 Key: first fully separate “build once” from “query many” — keep the index resident, loaded only once at startup; then make the request path fully async, pool and reuse external connections, warm up at boot, and add rate limiting for peaks. (1) Find the avalanche's root cause: nine times out of ten it's building / loading the index inside the request handler — every request re-chunks and re-embeds, crushing CPU and memory with repeated rebuilds. Hoist it to module level / a startup hook so globally you load_index_from_storage once and reuse a resident query engine. (2) Fully async request path: use async def + await qe.aquery(q) (from L24), and never slip a synchronous blocking call into an async view or it still jams the event loop. (3) Connection pooling / reuse: use pools for the vector DB and LLM clients instead of a fresh connection per request, and batch embedding / LLM calls where possible. (4) Cure cold start: lean on persistence (from L11) so startup is a seconds-long load, not a rebuild; then warm up — fire one dummy query to heat models / caches / connections before the readiness check lets traffic in. (5) Rate limit + timeouts: cap concurrency and time out slow requests so peaks queue or shed instead of toppling the box; pair with horizontal replicas sharing one persisted store. Finally use L23's traces to confirm whether the bottleneck is retrieval, the LLM, or I/O wait.
🎯 2. 服务上线只是开始。跑起来之后，你怎么持续保证质量，不让它悄悄退化、出了错也能查、还能在关键处兜底？Going live is just the start. Once it's running, how do you sustain quality — keep it from silently regressing, stay able to debug failures, and have a fallback at the critical points?
看参考要点Show key points 点击展开expand
🔑 重点：把全书攒下的能力串成一条上线后的质量闭环——L22 回归闸在发布前挡退化、L23 trace 在出错时定位、L25 护栏在运行时自动兜底、必要时L33 HITL 在不可逆处让人拍板；越靠后越贵，所以越靠后用得越省。① 发布前——L22 回归闸：用 BatchEvalRunner 跑一组带标准答案的题，把 Faithfulness / 命中率聚成通过率，低于阈值就挡下这次发布，别让改 prompt / 换模型悄悄把质量带崩。② 出错时——L23 可观测：全链路埋 trace，一条答错的 query 能摊开看检索召回了什么、rerank 留了谁、LLM 烧了多少 token，分清是检索没召到还是生成没用好，而不是瞎改。③ 运行时——L25 护栏：输入挡注入 / 越权，输出挡 PII / 有害 / 离题，机器能判的自动拦，根本不惊动人。④ 灰色地带——L33 HITL：规则判不了、又不可逆 / 高风险的，才在闸口让人点头。⑤ 持续校准：把线上 trace 里暴露的坏例子回灌进 L22 的评估集，让回归闸越用越严——质量不是上线那天的快照，而是一条测→观→兜→改的闭环。🔑 Key: stitch the book's capabilities into a post-launch quality loop — L22's regression gate blocks regressions before release, L23's traces localize failures, L25's guardrails auto-catch at runtime, and L33's HITL hands irreversible calls to a human when needed; each later layer is pricier, so each is used more sparingly. (1) Before release — L22 regression gate: run a labeled question set with BatchEvalRunner, aggregate Faithfulness / hit-rate into a pass rate, and block the release below threshold so a prompt edit / model swap can't quietly tank quality. (2) On failure — L23 observability: trace the whole chain so a wrong answer can be unfolded to see what retrieval returned, what rerank kept, how many tokens the LLM burned, telling a retrieval miss from poor generation instead of guessing. (3) At runtime — L25 guardrails: block injection / over-reach on input and PII / harmful / off-topic on output — what a machine can judge is auto-blocked and never bothers a human. (4) Gray zone — L33 HITL: only the irreversible / high-risk cases a rule can't settle go to a human nod. (5) Keep calibrating: feed the bad cases surfaced in production traces back into L22's eval set so the gate tightens over time — quality isn't a launch-day snapshot but a test → observe → guard → fix loop.
